<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="English">English</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=watermelon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: English">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="sister-wikipedia sister-project noprint floatright" style="border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 90%; background: #f9f9f9; width: 250px; padding: 4px; text-align: left;"><div style="float: left;"><figure class="mw-halign-none" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/44px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="44" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/66px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/88px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="103" data-file-height="94"></span><figcaption></figcaption></figure></div><div style="margin-left: 60px;">English <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> has an article on:<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b class="Latn" lang="en"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/watermelon" class="extiw" title="w:watermelon">watermelon</a></b></div></div><span class="interProject"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/watermelon" class="extiw" title="w:watermelon">Wikipedia </a></span></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=watermelon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the 1610s, a compound of <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/water#English" title="water">water</a></i> +â <i class="Latn mention" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/melon#English" title="melon">melon</a></i>. The meanings referring to environmentalists and behind schedule projects derive from the idea of having <a href="/wiki/green" title="green">green</a> (eco-friendly, on-schedule) outward appearance while being <a href="/wiki/red" title="red">red</a> (socialist, behind schedule) in a hidden way comparable to that of the fruit.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">Pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=watermelon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_English" class="extiw" title="w:British English">UK</a></span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Wiktionary:International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_pronunciation" title="Appendix:English pronunciation">key</a>)</sup>: <span class="IPA">/ËwÉËtÉËmÉlÉn/</span></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_English" class="extiw" title="w:American English">US</a></span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span> <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary:International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="Wiktionary:International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a><sup>(<a href="/wiki/Appendix:English_pronunciation" title="Appendix:English pronunciation">key</a>)</sup>: <span class="IPA">/ËwÉtÉÉ¹ËmÉlÉn/</span>, <span class="IPA">/ËwÉtÉÉ¹ËmÉlÉn/</span></li>
<li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r50165410">.mw-parser-output .k-player .k-attribution{visibility:hidden}</style><table class="audiotable" style="vertical-align: middle; display:inline-block; list-style:none;line-height: 1em; border-collapse:collapse;"><tbody><tr><td class="unicode audiolink" style="padding-right:5px; padding-left: 0;">Audio (US)</td><td class="audiofile"><span typeof="mw:File"><span><span class="mw-tmh-player audio" style="width:175px;"><audio id="mwe_player_0_placeholder" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="175" style="width:175px;" data-durationhint="1" data-mwtitle="en-us-watermelon.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" disabled="disabled" tabindex="-1"></audio><a class="mw-tmh-play" href="/wiki/File:en-us-watermelon.ogg" title="Play media" role="button"><span class="mw-tmh-play-icon"></span></a><span class="mw-tmh-duration mw-tmh-label" aria-label="1 second">0:01</span></span></span></span></td><td class="audiometa" style="font-size: 80%;">(<a href="/wiki/File:en-us-watermelon.ogg" title="File:en-us-watermelon.ogg">file</a>)</td></tr></tbody></table></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=watermelon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Noun">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">watermelon</strong> (<i><a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#countable" title="Appendix:Glossary">countable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#uncountable" title="Appendix:Glossary">uncountable</a></i>, <i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en"><a href="/wiki/watermelons#English" title="watermelons">watermelons</a></b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A plant of the species <i><a href="/wiki/Citrullus_lanatus" title="Citrullus lanatus">Citrullus lanatus</a></i>, bearing a <a href="/wiki/melon" title="melon">melon</a>-like fruit.</li>
<li>The fruit of the watermelon plant, having a green rind and watery flesh that is typically bright red when ripe and contains black <a href="/wiki/pip" title="pip">pips</a>.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="/wiki/derogatory" title="derogatory">derogatory</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="/wiki/Appendix:Glossary#slang" title="Appendix:Glossary">slang</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> An <a href="/wiki/environmentalist" title="environmentalist">environmentalist</a> with <a href="/wiki/socialist" title="socialist">socialist</a> leanings, an <a href="/wiki/ecosocialist" title="ecosocialist">ecosocialist</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;â¼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2010</b> August 7,  Robin McKie,  âMerchants of Doubt by Naomi Oreskes and Erik M Conwayâ, in  <cite>The Observer</cite>â<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.theguardian.com/books/2010/aug/08/merchants-of-doubt-oreskes-conway">[1]</a></sup>, <small><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/issn/0029-7712">âISSN</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">According to this distorted view of life, environmentalists are <b>watermelons</b> â green on the outside, red on the inside â who want to impose regulation, âthe slippery slope to socialismâ, on the use of tobacco, ozone-destroying chemicals and greenhouse gases.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/pinkish" title="pinkish">pinkish</a>-red <a href="/wiki/colour" title="colour">colour</a>, like that of watermelon flesh (also called watermelon pink).
<dl><dd><div class="color-panel">watermelon: <span style="background-color:#FDBCB4; display:inline-block; width:80px;">&nbsp;</span></div></dd></dl></li>
<li>A project that is <a href="/wiki/present" title="present">presented</a> as on <a href="/wiki/schedule" title="schedule">schedule</a> when it actually has parts that are <a href="/wiki/fall_behind" title="fall behind">falling behind</a>.
<span class="HQToggle"><a role="button" tabindex="0">quotations&nbsp;â¼</a></span><ul style="display: none;"><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2011</b> August 8,  Marc LÃ¶ffler,  â<b>Watermelon</b> Reportingâ, in  <cite>DZone</cite>â<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://dzone.com/articles/watermelon-reporting">[2]</a></sup>, AnswerHub:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">The nuts and bolts of any project are transparency. If the project status is transparent, the <b>watermelons</b> canât arise. If anybody is able to get the information, it will be difficult to hide something.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2015</b> September 17,  Ken Burrell,  âWatch out for <b>watermelons</b> in project reportsâ, in  <cite>LinkedIn</cite>â<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/watch-out-watermelons-project-reports-ken-burrell">[3]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">As a PMO [project management officer], wherever I see <b>watermelon</b> reporting, I encourage the PM [project manager] to be brave and honest enough to ask for help.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li>
<li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>2021</b> April 24,  Sumir Karayi,  âCombatting the <b>Watermelon</b> Effect to Improve Digital Experienceâ, in  <cite>CIO</cite>â<sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20210605175839/https://www.cio.com/article/3617909/combatting-the-watermelon-effect-to-improve-digital-experience.html">[4]</a></sup>, IDG Communications, archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.cio.com/article/3617909/combatting-the-watermelon-effect-to-improve-digital-experience.html">the original</a> on <span class="mw-formatted-date" title="2021-06-05">5 June 2021</span>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">[see title]</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
